It guarantees exactly once\\n32: // invocation of the provided notify functions.\\n33: type Handler struct {\\n34: \\tnotify []func()\\n35: \\tfinal  func(os.Signal)\\n36: \\tonce   sync.Once\\n37: }\\n38: \\n39: // New creates a new handler that guarantees all notify functions are run after the critical\\n40: // section exits (or is interrupted by the OS), then invokes the final handler. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go`. The `SetupSignalContext()` function (line 40-55) registers signal handlers using `signal.Notify(shutdownHandler, shutdownSignals...)` at line 46. The `shutdownSignals` are defined in platform-specific files: `signal_posix.go` registers `os.Interrupt` and `syscall.SIGTERM` for Unix-like systems, while `signal_windows.go` registers only `os.Interrupt`.\\n\\n**Shutdown Mechanism:**\\nThe signal handler creates a buffered channel with capacity 2 (line 43), allowing it to accept a first signal for graceful shutdown and a second signal for immediate termination. A background goroutine (lines 47-52) listens on this channel: the first signal triggers context cancellation via `cancel()`, and a second signal calls `os.Exit(1)` to forcefully terminate the process.\\n\\n**Cleanup Ordering:**\\nFor ordered cleanup, Kubernetes provides the interrupt handler pattern in `pkg/util/interrupt/interrupt.go`. The `Handler` struct (lines 33-37) maintains a list of notification functions and a final handler. The `Run()` method (lines 77-93) ensures cleanup functions execute after the critical section, either when it completes normally or when interrupted by OS signals. The `Signal()` method (lines 62-72) guarantees exactly-once invocation of cleanup functions using `sync.Once`, then invokes the final handler.\\n\\nThe `staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/pkg/signals/signal.go` implements an alternative with context-based approach, returning `context.Context` from `SetupSignalHandler()` that is cancelled on the first signal.\\n\\n### Prometheus/Prometheus\\n\\n**Signal Handler Registration:**\\nPrometheus registers signal handlers in `cmd/prometheus/main.go` (lines 1154-1155) using `signal.Notify(term, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)`. The signal handler is part of a larger actor-model orchestration using the `oklog/run` package's `run.Group`.\\n\\n**Graceful Shutdown Flow:**\\nThe termination handler (lines 1151-1177) follows this flow:\\n1. Signal reception triggers context cancellation via the cancel channel\\n2. The `webHandler.SetReady(web.Stopping)` marks the service as stopping (line 1173)\\n3. A notification is added to alert users (line 1174)\\n4. Each component responds to the cancel signal and executes its stop function\\n\\n**Cleanup Ordering & Connection Draining:**\\nPrometheus demonstrates explicit drain-before-stop ordering in the notifier system. In `notifier/sendloop.go` (lines 124-150), the `stop()` method checks `DrainOnShutdown` flag (line 129). If enabled, it calls `drainQueue()` (lines 146-149) which processes remaining queue items before cleanup (lines 137-142). This ensures pending Alertmanager notifications are sent before the service terminates.\\n\\nThe web handler shutdown in `web/web.go` (lines 766-768) demonstrates graceful HTTP shutdown: when the context is cancelled, `httpSrv.Shutdown(ctx)` is called to drain in-flight connections before closing the server.\\n\\nThe `notifier/manager.go` `Run()` method (lines 200-215) handles manager shutdown by stopping all send loops, which triggers their drain functions, ensuring a clean shutdown sequence.\\n\\n### Grafana/Grafana\\n\\n**Signal Handler Registration:**\\nGrafana's operator implementations in `pkg/operators/provisioning/` use a straightforward signal handling pattern. Files like `connection_operator.go` (lines 36-42), `repo_operator.go` (lines 39-45), `jobs_operator.go` (lines 48-60), and `zanzana_folder_reconciler.go` (lines 48-60) all register signals using `signal.Notify(sigChan, syscall.SIGINT, syscall.SIGTERM)`.\\n\\n**Graceful Shutdown:**\\nAll Grafana operators follow an identical pattern:\\n1. Create a context with cancellation (line 33/36/48: `context.WithCancel(context.Background())`)\\n2. Register signal handler in a non-blocking goroutine that calls `cancel()` on signal receipt\\n3. Start informer factories and controllers that respect the cancellation context\\n4. The `informerFactory.Start(ctx.Done())` and controllers listen to context cancellation\\n5. Upon signal reception, the cancel function triggers orchestrated shutdown of all controllers\\n\\nThis context-based approach ensures that all active goroutines and controllers gracefully wind down when any SIGINT or SIGTERM is received.\\n\\n## Common Patterns Across All Three Services\\n\\n**Signal Handler Registration:** All three use Go's standard `os/signal.Notify()` to register handlers for SIGTERM and SIGINT (with Interrupt on Windows).\\n\\n**Graceful Shutdown Mechanism:** \\n- Kubernetes: Context cancellation with buffered channel for second signal handling\\n- Prometheus: Actor-model with run.Group orchestrating component shutdowns\\n- Grafana: Context-based cancellation propagated through informer factories\\n\\n**Cleanup Ordering:**\\n- Kubernetes: `sync.Once` ensures cleanup executes exactly once in the correct order\\n- Prometheus: Explicit drain patterns (notifier queue draining before service stop, HTTP connection draining)\\n- Grafana: Context propagation ensures controllers stop in order of dependency\\n\\n**Second Signal Handling:** All services handle forceful termination on second signal - Kubernetes and sample-controller explicitly call `os.Exit(1)`, while Prometheus and Grafana rely on the OS behavior when signal handlers are removed.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2502,"cache_read_input_tokens":66032,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2502},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"8fa00bb1-e428-4c58-b63b-85ae1cac2fd0","uuid":"8784a106-4bef-4158-a796-7e2a8facc6bf"}
